<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">We consider here worst-case analysis of backscatter from passive radio frequency identification (RFID) tags. The basis is a figure of merit “B” to relate link power at reader ports to tag circuit parameters. A minimum bound for received monostatic backscatter can be determined by inspection from measured B. The bound is general for narrowband signals in any causal linear propagation. For an assembled tag, this minimum varies only with reader transmit power, tag antenna tuning, and chip power sensitivity of different commands. To validate this model, we propose a backscatter calibration device to enable measurements with estimated 0.5 dB uncertainty. We then demonstrate how the minimum bound can inform reader sensitivity specification to help ensure reliable inventory performance.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Passive ultrahigh-frequency (UHF) radio frequency identification (RFID) is a well-known and widely deployed use of RF energy harvesting. This brings significant attention to forward (reader to tag) links. Far-field systems' return (tag to reader) links, in contrast, are often neglected. These use an unusual backscattering mechanism that was introduced in the 1930s for aircraft transponders <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1, p. 7]</a>, the 1940s for espionage <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, the 1950s for antenna measurements <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, and only later in the 1970s for inventory management <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>.</p><p>Signaling in each link, illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, is detailed in EPC Global “Class 1 Gen 2” and ISO 18000-6C standards <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. A tag chip absorbs energy from a carrier through its antenna within 860 to 960 MHz until a reader transmits a modulated request for data. The chip then time varies the impedance loading the antenna, encoding a reply into modulation sidebands reflected back to the reader. This implementation of modulated scattering is known as load modulation. In this paper, “backscatter” refers to the reflected modulation available for reception at a reader port.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Two links of half-duplex ISO 18000-6C RFID communication. (a) Forward link, in which a reader sends a modulated request to a tag, which rectifies the incident wave to power its circuitry. (b) Return link, in which the tag reflects a modulated reply to the reader.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>Continued tag improvements have increased the range at which they can respond to readers. However, farther away, readers receive weaker backscatter. This tightens reader sensitivity requirements <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a> and increases vulnerability to interference <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. Reader specification and design for adequate sensitivity, which needs robust analysis of tag backscatter in realistic environments, is therefore becoming more important.</p><p>Previous work has characterized the scattering performance of a tag with “differential radar cross section (RCS)” (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma_{\Delta}</span><script type="math/tex">\sigma_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, sometimes known as “<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta {\rm RCS}</span><script type="math/tex">\Delta {\rm RCS}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>” <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a> or simply “RCS” <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1, p. 322]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>. Response power in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma_{\Delta}</span><script type="math/tex">\sigma_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is exclusively in modulation sidebands reflected around the carrier, proportional to tag antenna gain and circuit modulation efficiency.</p><p>In practice, current tag datasheets do not give <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma_{\Delta}</span><script type="math/tex">\sigma_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Specifying reader sensitivity therefore requires either good fortune or testing by each user. Standardized performance and conformance tests <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a> yield approximately 2 dB of uncertainty <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a>. Complete tests of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma_{\Delta}</span><script type="math/tex">\sigma_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> require sweeping across six degrees of freedom (DOF) in incident and scattered wave orientations, which may not be practical for low-cost, mass-produced tags.</p><p>Even well-measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma_{\Delta}</span><script type="math/tex">\sigma_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> leaves difficulty modeling realistic return links. In fading environments, modulation efficiency is meaningful <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>, but use of the tag's antenna gain pattern measured in free space becomes complicated. Few works have addressed indoor backscatter fading theory <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a>, and empirical data is scant <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_1">[16]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_1">[17]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_1">[18]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_1">[19]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_1">[20]</a>. Fading behavior is complicated further by the nonlinearity of tag responses with incident power.</p><p>Here, we propose a straightforward alternative for test and analysis of realistic monostatic return links. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Sections II</a> and <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">III</a> formulate a power parameter with network theory, assuming reciprocity as <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>. The result is equivalent to the parameter of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_1">[21]</a> for tag fingerprinting and near-field sensing, expanded to include effects of tag load compression and reader mismatch. To experimentally validate the theory with small uncertainty, <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a> introduces a measurement testbed with a new calibration method. Finally, <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec6" class="fulltext-link">Section VI</a> gives example test data with application to worst case return link analysis for ensuring reliable communication.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Network Model of Power Harvesting</h2></div><p>Here, we describe forward link operation in the general case with network theory. These expressions describe well-understood properties of this link, but we need to state and define them here to be able to express the limitations of the backscatter model in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>.</p><p>A network model of interaction between a reader and tag is illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>, following <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_2">[12]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_2">[22]</a>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{S}</span><script type="math/tex">{S}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameter network <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E</span><script type="math/tex">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula> contains all transmission effects between reader ports and a tag chip, including cables, antennas, and propagation effects. Ports 1 and 2 of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E</span><script type="math/tex">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are attached to the monostatic or bistatic reader. Port 3 is the interface between the tag's chip and antenna. The reader transmits into ports 1 or 2; each is assumed not to load the other.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Linearized <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{S}</span><script type="math/tex">{S}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameter model of reader and tag signaling. In return modulation, the tag chip switches between <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{L, R}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{L, R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (impedances <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{L,R}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{L,R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). The tag antenna, loaded slightly by the reader, presents <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) to the chip. Backscatter at ports 1 and 2 is produced by interaction between the tag antenna and the switching chip load.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>This paper contains <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{S}</span><script type="math/tex">{S}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameter traveling waves and not power waves often found in RFID literature. These incident and reflected waves are <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">a,b=V/Z_{0}^{1/2}</span><script type="math/tex">a,b=V/Z_{0}^{1/2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, for rms voltage wave phasors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V</span><script type="math/tex">V</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Normalization impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{0}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is assumed to be real and the same at all ports. The reflection coefficient looking into some <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z</span><script type="math/tex">Z</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is then <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho =(Z_{0}-Z)/(Z_{0}+Z)</span><script type="math/tex">\rho =(Z_{0}-Z)/(Z_{0}+Z)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Dependence on frequency in this paper is implicit and not shown for any <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z,\,\rho</span><script type="math/tex">Z,\,\rho</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, or power.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. Nonlinear Operating Point</h3><p>Realistic nonlinear <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{L}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{R}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> vary with power and feed impedance. Most generally, the feed <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> must be considered both at the carrier and its harmonics. We neglect these harmonics, however, under the assumption that they are filtered at the chip output to avoid out-of-band reflections. Therefore, we use “large-signal” network parameters at the carrier frequency. This requires a power quantity to use as an operating point. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is impractical to measure, so instead we detail how remotely measurable operating point <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}</span><script type="math/tex">\bar {p}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be defined relative to the turn-on power.</p><p>Available transmit power from the reader (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) is related to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{S}</span><script type="math/tex">{S}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameter traveling waves from either port (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">a_{1,2}</span><script type="math/tex">a_{1,2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) with <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_2a">[23]</a> <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert a_{1,2}\vert ^{2} = P_{\rm tx} (1-\vert \rho_{I1, I2}\vert ^{2}).\eqno{\hbox{(1)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\vert a_{1,2}\vert ^{2} = P_{\rm tx} (1-\vert \rho_{I1, I2}\vert ^{2}).\eqno{\hbox{(1)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\vert a_{1,2}\vert ^{2} = P_{\rm tx} (1-\vert \rho_{I1, I2}\vert ^{2}).\eqno{\hbox{(1)}}</span></span></disp-formula> Likewise, available power from the tag antenna <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is related to the wave into the antenna <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">b_{3}</span><script type="math/tex">b_{3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with <disp-formula id="deqn2" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert b_{3}\vert ^{2} = P_{\rm ant} {(1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2})} \eqno{\hbox{(2)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\vert b_{3}\vert ^{2} = P_{\rm ant} {(1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2})} \eqno{\hbox{(2)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\vert b_{3}\vert ^{2} = P_{\rm ant} {(1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2})} \eqno{\hbox{(2)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E_{33}</span><script type="math/tex">E_{33}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> loaded through <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E</span><script type="math/tex">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by the reader. The exact expression for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is long and uninformative, but <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{\rm ant} \approx E_{33}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{\rm ant} \approx E_{33}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> if the reader is well matched or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E</span><script type="math/tex">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula> transmission coefficients are small. These <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are therefore related to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E_{31}=b_{3}/a_{1}</span><script type="math/tex">E_{31}=b_{3}/a_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E_{32}=b_{3}/a_{2}</span><script type="math/tex">E_{32}=b_{3}/a_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by <disp-formula id="deqn3" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{{P_{\rm ant}}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} = \vert E_{31,32}\vert ^{2} {{1-\vert \rho_{I1, I2}\vert ^{2}}\over {1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(3)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">{{P_{\rm ant}}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} = \vert E_{31,32}\vert ^{2} {{1-\vert \rho_{I1, I2}\vert ^{2}}\over {1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(3)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{{P_{\rm ant}}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} = \vert E_{31,32}\vert ^{2} {{1-\vert \rho_{I1, I2}\vert ^{2}}\over {1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(3)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>State-of-the-art commercial tag chip sensitivity (minimum peak power delivered for turn-on) is on the order of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L0}=-\hbox{15 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L0}=-\hbox{15 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This is far above the noise floor, so the link is limited by power and not by signal-to-noise ratio (SNR). As a result, there is a sharply defined power available from the tag antenna, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ant0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm ant0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, where the tag load is at the turn-on threshold. Any <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be expressed relative to this as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ant}= \bar {p} P_{\rm ant0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm ant}= \bar {p} P_{\rm ant0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Excess power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}</span><script type="math/tex">\bar {p}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be interpreted as “power level relative to turn-on.” If it is expressed in decibels, it can be read as “dB above turn-on.”</p><p>A reader with adequate sensitivity can remotely detect whether a tag is on by detecting backscattered power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at some power level<disp-formula id="deqn4" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}=0, \qquad\hbox{for }P_{\rm tx} &lt; P_{\rm tx0} \eqno{\hbox{(4)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">P_{\rm bs}=0, \qquad\hbox{for }P_{\rm tx} &lt; P_{\rm tx0} \eqno{\hbox{(4)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">P_{\rm bs}=0, \qquad\hbox{for }P_{\rm tx} &lt; P_{\rm tx0} \eqno{\hbox{(4)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the minimum power to turn on. Because all terms on the right-hand side of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn3" href="#deqn3" class="fulltext-link">(3)</a> are linear, they are independent of operating point: <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ant}/P_{\rm tx}=P_{\rm ant0}/P_{\rm tx0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm ant}/P_{\rm tx}=P_{\rm ant0}/P_{\rm tx0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Therefore<disp-formula id="deqn5" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}= {{P_{\rm tx}}\over {P_{\rm tx0}}}= {{P_{\rm ant}}\over {P_{\rm ant0}}}\eqno{\hbox{(5)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\bar {p}= {{P_{\rm tx}}\over {P_{\rm tx0}}}= {{P_{\rm ant}}\over {P_{\rm ant0}}}\eqno{\hbox{(5)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\bar {p}= {{P_{\rm tx}}\over {P_{\rm tx0}}}= {{P_{\rm ant}}\over {P_{\rm ant0}}}\eqno{\hbox{(5)}}</span></span></disp-formula>showing that the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}</span><script type="math/tex">\bar {p}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> operating point has analagous meaning at the reader and inside the tag.</p><p>This concept is exploited (though not explained) in ISO 18047-6 <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2a">[11]</a>, prescribing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma_{\Delta}</span><script type="math/tex">\sigma_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> measurements at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}=120\%</span><script type="math/tex">\bar {p}=120\%</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (0.8 dB). Because <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}</span><script type="math/tex">\bar {p}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> wirelessly permits insight into power levels inside the tag, it is the basis for linearity test and analysis in this paper as well.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b"><h3>B. Tag Match Efficiency</h3><p>The tag model shows the tag chip switching between a power harvesting rectifier load <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{L}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{S}</span><script type="math/tex">{S}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{L}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) and a more reflective modulation state <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{R}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{S}</span><script type="math/tex">{S}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{R}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). Realistic values are of the order of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{L} \approx (15-j150) \Omega</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{L} \approx (15-j150) \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{R}\approx (12.5-j100) \Omega</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{R}\approx (12.5-j100) \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_2b">[24]</a>. We focus here on <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{L}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which the chip presents most often to maximize time-averaged rectified power.</p><p>Available power from the antenna (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) is related to power delivered to the tag chip (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L} = P_{\rm ant} \eta_{L}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L} = P_{\rm ant} \eta_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{L}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the tag matching efficiency between the antenna and the chip <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref25" id="context_ref_25_2b">[25]</a> and is given as<disp-formula id="deqn6" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{\eta_{L}(\bar {p}) =&amp;\, {{(1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2})(1-\vert \rho_{L}(\bar {p})\vert ^{2})}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{\rm ant}\rho_{L}(\bar {p})\vert ^{2}}} \cr =&amp;\, {{4 {\rm \rm Re}\{Z_{L}(\bar {p})\} {\rm \rm Re}\{Z_{\rm ant}\}}\over {\left \vert {Z_{L}(\bar {p})+Z_{\rm ant}}\right \vert ^{2}}}. &amp;{\hbox{(6)}}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\eqalignno{\eta_{L}(\bar {p}) =&amp;\, {{(1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2})(1-\vert \rho_{L}(\bar {p})\vert ^{2})}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{\rm ant}\rho_{L}(\bar {p})\vert ^{2}}} \cr =&amp;\, {{4 {\rm \rm Re}\{Z_{L}(\bar {p})\} {\rm \rm Re}\{Z_{\rm ant}\}}\over {\left \vert {Z_{L}(\bar {p})+Z_{\rm ant}}\right \vert ^{2}}}. &amp;{\hbox{(6)}}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{\eta_{L}(\bar {p}) =&amp;\, {{(1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2})(1-\vert \rho_{L}(\bar {p})\vert ^{2})}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{\rm ant}\rho_{L}(\bar {p})\vert ^{2}}} \cr =&amp;\, {{4 {\rm \rm Re}\{Z_{L}(\bar {p})\} {\rm \rm Re}\{Z_{\rm ant}\}}\over {\left \vert {Z_{L}(\bar {p})+Z_{\rm ant}}\right \vert ^{2}}}. &amp;{\hbox{(6)}}}</span></span></disp-formula>If a chip and antenna are conjugate-matched, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{L}(\bar {p})= {\hbox {0 dB}}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{L}(\bar {p})= {\hbox {0 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and all available energy from the antenna is delivered to the chip.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2c"><h3>C. Transmission Link Loss</h3><p>Transducer gain expresses the fraction of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> absorbed by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{L}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> through <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E</span><script type="math/tex">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_2c">[23]</a> as <disp-formula id="deqn7" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{{P_{L}(\bar p)}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} = {{1-\vert \rho_{L}(\bar p)\vert ^{2}}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{\rm ant}\rho_{L}\vert ^{2}}} {{1-\vert \rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{1}\rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}} \vert E_{31}\vert ^{2}.\eqno{\hbox{(7)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">{{P_{L}(\bar p)}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} = {{1-\vert \rho_{L}(\bar p)\vert ^{2}}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{\rm ant}\rho_{L}\vert ^{2}}} {{1-\vert \rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{1}\rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}} \vert E_{31}\vert ^{2}.\eqno{\hbox{(7)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{{P_{L}(\bar p)}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} = {{1-\vert \rho_{L}(\bar p)\vert ^{2}}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{\rm ant}\rho_{L}\vert ^{2}}} {{1-\vert \rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{1}\rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}} \vert E_{31}\vert ^{2}.\eqno{\hbox{(7)}}</span></span></disp-formula>If the tag load's detuning effect on the reader antenna is small, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{1} \approx E_{11}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{1} \approx E_{11}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. With the reader transmit match coefficient, we have <disp-formula id="deqn8" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{\rm tx} = {{1-\vert \rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{1}\rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}} \eqno{\hbox{(8)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\eta_{\rm tx} = {{1-\vert \rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{1}\rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}} \eqno{\hbox{(8)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eta_{\rm tx} = {{1-\vert \rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{1}\rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}} \eqno{\hbox{(8)}}</span></span></disp-formula>and, from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn6" href="#deqn6" class="fulltext-link">(6)</a>, we obtain <disp-formula id="deqn9" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{{P_{L}(\bar p)}\over {P_{tx}}} = \eta_{tx} {{\eta_{L}(\bar p)}\over {1-\vert \rho_{ant}\vert ^{2}}} \vert E_{31}\vert ^{2}.\eqno{\hbox{(9)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">{{P_{L}(\bar p)}\over {P_{tx}}} = \eta_{tx} {{\eta_{L}(\bar p)}\over {1-\vert \rho_{ant}\vert ^{2}}} \vert E_{31}\vert ^{2}.\eqno{\hbox{(9)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{{P_{L}(\bar p)}\over {P_{tx}}} = \eta_{tx} {{\eta_{L}(\bar p)}\over {1-\vert \rho_{ant}\vert ^{2}}} \vert E_{31}\vert ^{2}.\eqno{\hbox{(9)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>It is now possible to express <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert E_{31}\vert ^{2}</span><script type="math/tex">\vert E_{31}\vert ^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> entirely with terms at the reader and tag interfaces and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar p</span><script type="math/tex">\bar p</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as <disp-formula id="deqn10" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert E_{31}\vert ^{2} = \bar p {{1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2}}\over {\eta_{\rm tx} \eta_{L0}}} {{P_{L0}}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} \eqno{\hbox{(10)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\vert E_{31}\vert ^{2} = \bar p {{1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2}}\over {\eta_{\rm tx} \eta_{L0}}} {{P_{L0}}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} \eqno{\hbox{(10)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\vert E_{31}\vert ^{2} = \bar p {{1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2}}\over {\eta_{\rm tx} \eta_{L0}}} {{P_{L0}}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} \eqno{\hbox{(10)}}</span></span></disp-formula>from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn9" href="#deqn9" class="fulltext-link">(9)</a>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L}=\eta_{L} P_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L}=\eta_{L} P_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L0}=\eta_{L0} P_{\rm ant0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L0}=\eta_{L0} P_{\rm ant0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Backscatter Model</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Formulation</h3><p>We begin with analysis of monostatic operation. During a tag response, time-varying traveling wave <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">b_{1,2} (t)</span><script type="math/tex">b_{1,2} (t)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (at ports 1 or 2) is reflected to the reader. This is an analytic signal corresponding to the modulated tag response. For bi-phase-shift-keyed (BPSK) RFID tag signaling, we idealize <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">b_{1,2}(t)</span><script type="math/tex">b_{1,2}(t)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as switching instantaneously between two states separated by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta b_{1,2}</span><script type="math/tex">\Delta b_{1,2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>The modulation power available to the reader is <disp-formula id="deqn11" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs} = \left ({{1}\over {4}}\right) {{\vert \Delta b_{1,2}\vert ^{2}}\over {1-\vert \rho_{1,2}\vert ^{2}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(11)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">P_{\rm bs} = \left ({{1}\over {4}}\right) {{\vert \Delta b_{1,2}\vert ^{2}}\over {1-\vert \rho_{1,2}\vert ^{2}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(11)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">P_{\rm bs} = \left ({{1}\over {4}}\right) {{\vert \Delta b_{1,2}\vert ^{2}}\over {1-\vert \rho_{1,2}\vert ^{2}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(11)}}</span></span></disp-formula>We assume here that the reader antenna reflection coefficients <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{1,2}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{1,2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are constant across the modulation bandwidth. The fast switching in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">b_{1,2}(t)</span><script type="math/tex">b_{1,2}(t)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> contains broad harmonic content, so this assumption introduces error for any physically realizable antenna. This error may be negligible for antennas with low dispersion and flat <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert \rho_{1,2}\vert</span><script type="math/tex">\vert \rho_{1,2}\vert</script></tex-math></inline-formula> over a broad bandwidth (relative to “most” power in the tag response power spectrum).</p><p>When excited by a steady <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">a_{1,2}</span><script type="math/tex">a_{1,2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, monostatic reader operation is equivalent to detecting changes in reflection coefficient, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta \rho_{\rm bs} = b_{1,2}/a_{1,2}</span><script type="math/tex">\Delta \rho_{\rm bs} = b_{1,2}/a_{1,2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Previous work <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_3a">[22]</a> related this to tag circuit parameters through propagation network <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E</span><script type="math/tex">E</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. At port 1, this is <disp-formula id="deqn12" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta \rho_{\rm bs} = E_{31}E_{13} {{\rho_{R}(\bar p)-\rho_{L}(\bar p)}\over {(1-\rho_{\rm ant}\rho_{L}(\bar p))(1-\rho_{\rm ant}\rho_{R}(\bar p))}}.\eqno{\hbox{(12)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\Delta \rho_{\rm bs} = E_{31}E_{13} {{\rho_{R}(\bar p)-\rho_{L}(\bar p)}\over {(1-\rho_{\rm ant}\rho_{L}(\bar p))(1-\rho_{\rm ant}\rho_{R}(\bar p))}}.\eqno{\hbox{(12)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\Delta \rho_{\rm bs} = E_{31}E_{13} {{\rho_{R}(\bar p)-\rho_{L}(\bar p)}\over {(1-\rho_{\rm ant}\rho_{L}(\bar p))(1-\rho_{\rm ant}\rho_{R}(\bar p))}}.\eqno{\hbox{(12)}}</span></span></disp-formula>The left-hand side of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn12" href="#deqn12" class="fulltext-link">(12)</a> is related to transmit and backscattered power with <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn11" href="#deqn11" class="fulltext-link">(11)</a> by <disp-formula id="deqn13" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert \Delta \rho_{\rm bs}\vert ^{2} = \left \vert {{\Delta b_{1}}\over {a_{1}}}\right \vert ^{2} = 4 {{P_{\rm bs}}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} {{\eta_{\rm rx}}\over {\eta_{\rm tx}}}\eqno{\hbox{(13)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\vert \Delta \rho_{\rm bs}\vert ^{2} = \left \vert {{\Delta b_{1}}\over {a_{1}}}\right \vert ^{2} = 4 {{P_{\rm bs}}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} {{\eta_{\rm rx}}\over {\eta_{\rm tx}}}\eqno{\hbox{(13)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\vert \Delta \rho_{\rm bs}\vert ^{2} = \left \vert {{\Delta b_{1}}\over {a_{1}}}\right \vert ^{2} = 4 {{P_{\rm bs}}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} {{\eta_{\rm rx}}\over {\eta_{\rm tx}}}\eqno{\hbox{(13)}}</span></span></disp-formula>with the reader receive match coefficient <disp-formula id="deqn14" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{\rm rx} = {{1-\vert \rho_{1}\vert ^{2}}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{1}\rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}} \eqno{\hbox{(14)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\eta_{\rm rx} = {{1-\vert \rho_{1}\vert ^{2}}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{1}\rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}} \eqno{\hbox{(14)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eta_{\rm rx} = {{1-\vert \rho_{1}\vert ^{2}}\over {\vert 1-\rho_{1}\rho_{I1}\vert ^{2}}} \eqno{\hbox{(14)}}</span></span></disp-formula>at port 1. Like <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{\rm tx},\,\eta_{\rm rx}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{\rm tx},\,\eta_{\rm rx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> approaches 0 dB for well-matched reader systems.</p><p>The right-hand side of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn12" href="#deqn12" class="fulltext-link">(12)</a> resembles modulation efficiency <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_3a">[12]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_3a">[26]</a> <disp-formula id="deqn15" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{\eta_{\rm mod}(\bar p)=&amp;\, {{(1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2})^{2} \vert src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{\eta_{\rm mod}(\bar p)=&amp;\, {{(1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert &amp;{\hbox{(15)}}}</span></span></disp-formula>For passive <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{L,R}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{L,R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, modulation efficiency is bound by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">0\leq \eta_{\rm mod} \leq (1+\sqrt {1-\eta_{L}})^{2}</span><script type="math/tex">0\leq \eta_{\rm mod} \leq (1+\sqrt {1-\eta_{L}})^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Combining <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn10" href="#deqn10" class="fulltext-link">(10)</a>, <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn13" href="#deqn13" class="fulltext-link">(13)</a>, and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn15" href="#deqn15" class="fulltext-link">(15)</a> into <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn12" href="#deqn12" class="fulltext-link">(12)</a> gives <disp-formula id="deqn16" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{{\eta_{\rm rx} P_{\rm bs}}\over {\eta_{tx} P_{\rm tx}}} = {{\bar {p}^{2}}\over {4}}\left ({{1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2}}\over {\eta_{\rm tx} \eta_{L0}}} {{P_{L0}}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} \right) ^{2} {{\eta_{\rm mod}(\bar p)}\over {(1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2})^{2}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(16)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">{{\eta_{\rm rx} P_{\rm bs}}\over {\eta_{tx} P_{\rm tx}}} = {{\bar {p}^{2}}\over {4}}\left ({{1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2}}\over {\eta_{\rm tx} \eta_{L0}}} {{P_{L0}}\over {P_{\rm tx}}} \right) ^{2} {{\eta_{\rm mod}(\bar p)}\over {(1-\vert \rho_{\rm ant}\vert ^{2})^{2}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(16)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{\rm ant},\,\eta_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{\rm ant},\,\eta_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> terms and substitute <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx} = P_{\rm tx0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx} = P_{\rm tx0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to define our figure of merit <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as <disp-formula id="deqn17" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{B(\eta_{L0}, P_{L0}, \eta_{\rm bs}(\bar p))=&amp;\, P_{\rm tx0} P_{\rm bs} \eta_{\rm rx}\eta_{\rm tx} \cr =&amp;\, \bar {p} \left ({{P_{L0}}\over {\eta_{L0}}}\right)^{2} {{\eta_{\rm mod}(\bar {p})}\over {4}}. &amp;{\hbox{(17)}}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\eqalignno{B(\eta_{L0}, P_{L0}, \eta_{\rm bs}(\bar p))=&amp;\, P_{\rm tx0} P_{\rm bs} \eta_{\rm rx}\eta_{\rm tx} \cr =&amp;\, \bar {p} \left ({{P_{L0}}\over {\eta_{L0}}}\right)^{2} {{\eta_{\rm mod}(\bar {p})}\over {4}}. &amp;{\hbox{(17)}}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{B(\eta_{L0}, P_{L0}, \eta_{\rm bs}(\bar p))=&amp;\, P_{\rm tx0} P_{\rm bs} \eta_{\rm rx}\eta_{\rm tx} \cr =&amp;\, \bar {p} \left ({{P_{L0}}\over {\eta_{L0}}}\right)^{2} {{\eta_{\rm mod}(\bar {p})}\over {4}}. &amp;{\hbox{(17)}}}</span></span></disp-formula>To the extent that these parameters are independent of the environment, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is independent of linear propagation effects at fixed frequency and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}</span><script type="math/tex">\bar {p}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Analysis for bistatic reader operation proceeds in the same fashion and yields the same <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In this case, however, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{tx0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{tx0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> refers to the reader's <i>receive</i> port, where it is the hypothetical available power necessary to turn on the tag. This incorporates loss in the scattering path. Forward-link path loss is encapsulated in excess power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}</span><script type="math/tex">\bar {p}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as through <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn10" href="#deqn10" class="fulltext-link">(10)</a>. If <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is approximately the same through both transmit and receive antennas, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> behaves approximately as in monostatic operation.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Interpretation</h3><p>Use of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> through <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn17" href="#deqn17" class="fulltext-link">(17)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn18" href="#deqn18" class="fulltext-link">(18)</a> applies to test and link analysis under the following conditions.
</p><ol><li><p>Loss between reader and tag antennas loaded with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{0}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are linear and causal with respect to power.</p></li><li><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{\rm rx}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{\rm rx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is flat across the backscatter bandwidth.</p></li><li><p>Tag turn-on is abrupt and repeatable at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for each frequency and command.</p></li><li><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{\rm rx}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{\rm rx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are independent of the tag.</p></li></ol>These assumptions are implicit in the remainder of the paper.<p></p><p>Inventory tracking by definition requires that a tag is attached to an object. Taking this as the dominant environmental effect on tag tuning, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be considered a parameter of a “tagged object.”</p><p>Complete tests with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> must investigate any physical effects that alter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as a function of frequency and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar p</span><script type="math/tex">\bar p</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Tag circuit efficiencies (and therefore <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) do not depend significantly on air protocol parameters <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_3b">[26]</a>. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is known to increase by several decibels for tag “write” operations, so <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is smallest for tag read operations (like queries and inventories). Tag antenna detuning may cause <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to either increase or decrease.</p><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is not equivalent to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma_{\Delta}</span><script type="math/tex">\sigma_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Like <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma_{\Delta}</span><script type="math/tex">\sigma_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, larger values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> suggest larger typical <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. However, while <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma_{\Delta}</span><script type="math/tex">\sigma_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> characterizes a tag in complete isolation, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> describes the tag under the condition that the environment allows turn-on. This is why <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> depends on <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{L0}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{L0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>—they limit the maximum forward-link loss and therefore the maximum monostatic backscatter loss.</p><p>One interpretation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is as a balance between forward and return links. Increasing transmission loss requires greater <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to turn on the tag. Correspondingly, the loss is reciprocal, so backscattered power received by the reader falls. Nature therefore maintains a tradeoff between these two links. In a fixed tag tuning state, changes in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are of equal and opposite magnitude. Increasing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar p</span><script type="math/tex">\bar p</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases power available power for scattering by the tag and typically the backscatter received by the reader.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3c"><h3>C. Lower Bound for Monostatic Backscatter</h3><p>The link balance imposed by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> leads to its simplest and most powerful application to link analysis: the weakest backscattered power a monostatic reader can receive from a tag that is “on.” Since <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}</span><script type="math/tex">\bar {p}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> above turn-on, the minimum nonzero backscattered power occurs at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}= {\hbox {0 dB}}</span><script type="math/tex">\bar {p}= {\hbox {0 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The corresponding minimum bound to backscattered power is <disp-formula id="deqn18" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{\rm bs}] {(\hbox{dBm})} = \, [B\vert_{\bar {p}= {\hbox {0 dB}}} {(\hbox{dBm})^{2}}]-[P_{\rm tx} {(\hbox{dBm})}].\eqno{\hbox{(18)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\min [P_{\rm bs}] {(\hbox{dBm})} = \, [B\vert_{\bar {p}= {\hbox {0 dB}}} {(\hbox{dBm})^{2}}]-[P_{\rm tx} {(\hbox{dBm})}].\eqno{\hbox{(18)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\min [P_{\rm bs}] {(\hbox{dBm})} = \, [B\vert_{\bar {p}= {\hbox {0 dB}}} {(\hbox{dBm})^{2}}]-[P_{\rm tx} {(\hbox{dBm})}].\eqno{\hbox{(18)}}</span></span></disp-formula>Here, “<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\hbox{dBm})^{2}</span><script type="math/tex">(\hbox{dBm})^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>” is “dB relative to one square milliwatt” <disp-formula id="deqn19" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B {(\hbox{dBm})^{2}} = 10 \log_{10} {{B {(\hbox{mW})^{2}}}\over {1 (\hbox{mW})^{2}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(19)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">B {(\hbox{dBm})^{2}} = 10 \log_{10} {{B {(\hbox{mW})^{2}}}\over {1 (\hbox{mW})^{2}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(19)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">B {(\hbox{dBm})^{2}} = 10 \log_{10} {{B {(\hbox{mW})^{2}}}\over {1 (\hbox{mW})^{2}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(19)}}</span></span></disp-formula>Use of this unit is nonstandard, but allows <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</span><script type="math/tex">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to be determined from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> data “by inspection” by simply subtracting <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in dBm.</p><p>Because they are proportional, trends in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at turn-on are the same for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</span><script type="math/tex">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> through <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn18" href="#deqn18" class="fulltext-link">(18)</a>. For example, detuning that reduces <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> reduces <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</span><script type="math/tex">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by the same amount. Likewise, measurement uncertainty in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> contributes the same uncertainty toward <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</span><script type="math/tex">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>As a result, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</span><script type="math/tex">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of an assembled tag varies only with tag antenna tuning, frequency, and whether the tag reads or writes. A link margin may be subtracted from estimates of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</span><script type="math/tex">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> when specifying reader sensitivity to account for detuning effects.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Design of a Backscatter Testbed</h2></div><p>The focus of this section is the design of a testbed to measure <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> over the air with low uncertainty. Remote measurements of a tag's <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> require measurements of transmit power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and backscattered power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. To this end, we introduce a method to generate reference backscatter through a coupler to calibrate detected tag backscatter for accurate <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Design Overview</h3><p>The testbed is described in the block diagram of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a>. An interrogator transmits power and modulated query requests. Measurements use the circuit of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a> to calibrate results: coupled power measurements give <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and reference modulation reflected to the input of the coupler calibrates <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from the device under test (DUT). \</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>(a) Test setup topology, with modulated power measurements of tag and reference scatter are referenced to the indicated calibration plane. (b) Calibration circuit block diagram.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>An antenna on the right, selected with the transfer switch shown left of the calibration plane, transmits interrogation to the DUT. A spectrum analyzer detects backscatter through the receive antenna. Repeating measurements in each transfer switch state gives two bistatic measurements of turn-on power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and therefore two results for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The two values are averaged together to reduce noise.</p><p>The bistatic antenna topology maximizes carrier transmit/receive isolation. If the carrier at the spectrum analyzer is significantly stronger than the backscattered modulation, maintaining instrument linearity may require more attenuation, reducing backscatter measurement SNR and increasing noise uncertainty. Isolation between the two antennas is better than 45 dB across 860–960 MHz in the unloaded anechoic environment and better than 30 dB when the chamber is loaded with a large metal plate.</p><p>The spectrum analyzer and interrogator each have return loss greater than 25 dB, and the calibration circuit loaded by the antennas has return loss greater than 15 dB, so mismatch errors (and the discrepancy introduced by switching between the inputs) are below 0.06 dB (1.5%).</p><p>A monostatic system could also be used, but would require an antenna with return loss greater than 30 dB over the test bandwidth or the additional complexity of a carrier cancellation circuit (e.g., <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_4a">[27]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_4a">[28]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_4a">[29]</a>).</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Signals and Detection</h3><p>We use a commercial RFID test instrument to generate interrogation signals. Tests in this paper use the signaling parameters detailed in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>. Each is approximately midway between the extrema permitted by <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_4b">[5]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>Test Signal Parameters<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table I" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p><p>Average power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ref}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the coupled interrogation wave during tag backscatter is gated as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(a)</a>. Turn-on and backscatter performance measured this way has been shown to be nearly independent of many modulation and coding parameters of the interrogation signal <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_4b">[26]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Illustration of gating applied to (a) coupled transmit power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ref}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and (b)DUT and reference backscatter baseband voltages <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm dut}</span><script type="math/tex">V_{\rm dut}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm ref}</span><script type="math/tex">V_{\rm ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Forward-link transmit modulation is shown coupled in (a) and leaked in (b) before measurements (performed during the shaded periods).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>Commercial readers detect via in-phase and quadrature (IQ) demodulation of backscatter voltage. Likewise, our testbed detects demodulated IQ with a spectrum analyzer, gated as in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(b)</a>. The demodulation bandwidth is set to 10 MHz, which is much larger than the 640-kHz maximum base link frequency (BLF) to shorten transient ringing at pulse edges. Averaged measurements of the demodulated complex voltages between neighboring modulation states are recorded as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta V</span><script type="math/tex">\Delta V</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Uncalibrated measurements of DUT and reference modulation are recorded as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert \Delta V_{\rm dut}\vert</span><script type="math/tex">\vert \Delta V_{\rm dut}\vert</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert \Delta V_{\rm ref}\vert</span><script type="math/tex">\vert \Delta V_{\rm ref}\vert</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4c"><h3>C. Calibration Procedure</h3><p>Transmit power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> into either port is measured by directional coupler in the usual way. All ports of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S</span><script type="math/tex">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the power sensor are matched to greater than 30-dB return loss across 860–960 MHz, so mismatch is neglected. The coupling factors <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{1}=-20 \log_{10}{\vert S_{31}\vert }</span><script type="math/tex">C_{1}=-20 \log_{10}{\vert S_{31}\vert }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{2}=-20 \log_{10}{\vert S_{32}\vert }</span><script type="math/tex">C_{2}=-20 \log_{10}{\vert S_{32}\vert }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are measured by network analyzer. The power meter reading <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ref}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> then gives transmit power as <disp-formula id="deqn20" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx} {(\hbox{dBm})}=P_{\rm ref} {(\hbox{dBm})}+ C_{1,2}\eqno{\hbox{(20)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">P_{\rm tx} {(\hbox{dBm})}=P_{\rm ref} {(\hbox{dBm})}+ C_{1,2}\eqno{\hbox{(20)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">P_{\rm tx} {(\hbox{dBm})}=P_{\rm ref} {(\hbox{dBm})}+ C_{1,2}\eqno{\hbox{(20)}}</span></span></disp-formula>inserting the relevant coupling factor for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{1,2}</span><script type="math/tex">C_{1,2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Measurement at DUT turn-on gives <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Reference backscatter is achieved by modulating the solid-state switch in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S</span><script type="math/tex">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with a pulse generator set to the DUT BLF. It modulates after each DUT response until the interrogator stops emitting a CW tone. Sidebands about a carrier input into ports 1 or 2 are reflected back into both input ports, enabling monostatic or bistatic use.</p><p>In selecting couplers for this application, the choice of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">C_{1,2}</span><script type="math/tex">C_{1,2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> affects only dynamic range; the balance between them is not important. High directivity is significant to minimize errors in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (as in any coupled power measurement). These errors are within <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\pm \hbox{0.06 dB}</span><script type="math/tex">\pm \hbox{0.06 dB}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, determined after sweeping phase shift on a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert \rho \vert =-\hbox{10 dB}</span><script type="math/tex">\vert \rho \vert =-\hbox{10 dB}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> coupler load.</p><p>We perform bistatic calibration by measuring <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta \tau_{\rm ref}</span><script type="math/tex">\Delta \tau_{\rm ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> between the coupler inputs with a network analyzer, at the reference plane in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a>. The reference switching state is set with a dc voltage supply. We validate results by computing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta \tau_{\rm ref}</span><script type="math/tex">\Delta \tau_{\rm ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from measured parameters on the right-hand side of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn12" href="#deqn12" class="fulltext-link">(12)</a>, shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. Results agree to within 0.06 dB. We estimate the total uncertainty of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert \Delta \tau_{\rm ref}\vert</span><script type="math/tex">\vert \Delta \tau_{\rm ref}\vert</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 0.25 dB based on analysis of manufacturer specifications.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Network analyzer calibration measurement of the change in transmission coefficient <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta \tau_{\rm ref}</span><script type="math/tex">\Delta \tau_{\rm ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> through the reference load modulation device of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a>.
