The “validation” measurement is computed from measurements of each term of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn12" href="#deqn12" class="fulltext-link">(12)</a>, with separate incident and return transmission coefficients.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>Reference backscattered power, including <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{\rm tx, rx}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{\rm tx, rx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, is <disp-formula id="deqn21" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs, ref}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{\rm rx} \,{(\hbox{dBm})}=[P_{\rm tx}\,{(\hbox{dBm})}] + 10 \log_{10} {{\vert \Delta \tau_{\rm ref}\vert ^{2}}\over {4}} \eqno{\hbox{(21)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">P_{\rm bs, ref}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{\rm rx} \,{(\hbox{dBm})}=[P_{\rm tx}\,{(\hbox{dBm})}] + 10 \log_{10} {{\vert \Delta \tau_{\rm ref}\vert ^{2}}\over {4}} \eqno{\hbox{(21)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">P_{\rm bs, ref}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{\rm rx} \,{(\hbox{dBm})}=[P_{\rm tx}\,{(\hbox{dBm})}] + 10 \log_{10} {{\vert \Delta \tau_{\rm ref}\vert ^{2}}\over {4}} \eqno{\hbox{(21)}}</span></span></disp-formula>with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> calibrated from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn20" href="#deqn20" class="fulltext-link">(20)</a>.</p><p>Reference and DUT backscatter have narrow bandwidth about the same carrier, so linear, frequency-dependent losses are assumed to be the same for each. A calibration factor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">K</span><script type="math/tex">K</script></tex-math></inline-formula> encapsulating these effects can be determined from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta V_{\rm ref}</span><script type="math/tex">\Delta V_{\rm ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as <disp-formula id="deqn22" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">K {({\hbox {dB}})}=20 \log_{10} {\vert \Delta V_{\rm ref}\vert }-[P_{\rm bs, ref}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{\rm rx} {(\hbox{dBm})}].\eqno{\hbox{(22)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">K {({\hbox {dB}})}=20 \log_{10} {\vert \Delta V_{\rm ref}\vert }-[P_{\rm bs, ref}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{\rm rx} {(\hbox{dBm})}].\eqno{\hbox{(22)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">K {({\hbox {dB}})}=20 \log_{10} {\vert \Delta V_{\rm ref}\vert }-[P_{\rm bs, ref}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{\rm rx} {(\hbox{dBm})}].\eqno{\hbox{(22)}}</span></span></disp-formula>Backscattered power from the DUT, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, is then <disp-formula id="deqn23" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{rx} =20 \log_{10}{\vert \Delta V_{\rm dut}\vert }+[K {({\hbox {dB}})]}.\eqno{\hbox{(23)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">P_{\rm bs}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{rx} =20 \log_{10}{\vert \Delta V_{\rm dut}\vert }+[K {({\hbox {dB}})]}.\eqno{\hbox{(23)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">P_{\rm bs}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{rx} =20 \log_{10}{\vert \Delta V_{\rm dut}\vert }+[K {({\hbox {dB}})]}.\eqno{\hbox{(23)}}</span></span></disp-formula>Finally, the measured data give <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as <disp-formula id="deqn24" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{B \,{(\hbox{dBm})}^{2} =&amp;\, P_{tx0}\,{(\hbox{dBm})} + P_{\rm bs}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{\rm rx} \,{(\hbox{dBm})} \cr =&amp;\, 10 \log_{10} \left [P_{\rm tx0} {(\hbox{mW})}\times P_{\rm bs}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{\rm rx} {(\hbox{mW})}\right]. \cr &amp;&amp;{\hbox{(24)}}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">\eqalignno{B \,{(\hbox{dBm})}^{2} =&amp;\, P_{tx0}\,{(\hbox{dBm})} + P_{\rm bs}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{\rm rx} \,{(\hbox{dBm})} \cr =&amp;\, 10 \log_{10} \left [P_{\rm tx0} {(\hbox{mW})}\times P_{\rm bs}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{\rm rx} {(\hbox{mW})}\right]. \cr &amp;&amp;{\hbox{(24)}}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{B \,{(\hbox{dBm})}^{2} =&amp;\, P_{tx0}\,{(\hbox{dBm})} + P_{\rm bs}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{\rm rx} \,{(\hbox{dBm})} \cr =&amp;\, 10 \log_{10} \left [P_{\rm tx0} {(\hbox{mW})}\times P_{\rm bs}\eta_{\rm tx}\eta_{\rm rx} {(\hbox{mW})}\right]. \cr &amp;&amp;{\hbox{(24)}}}</span></span></disp-formula></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4d"><h3>D. Testbed Performance and Uncertainty</h3><p><a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a> lists performance parameters of the testbed illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>. Because <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is proportional to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, uncertainty in a tag's FOM contributes the same uncertainty to backscattered power estimates in link analysis.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table II </b>Testbed Specifications, 860–960 MHz<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table II" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p><p>System noise and linearity errors are estimated from input power sweeps of coupled interrogation power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm ref}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm ref}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and reference modulation in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>. Within the specified <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-\hbox{2}</span><script type="math/tex">-\hbox{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>–29-dBm transmit power range, these errors are within <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\pm {\hbox {0.1 dB}}</span><script type="math/tex">\pm {\hbox {0.1 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. We chose a commercial coaxial switch specified with low linearity errors, which is validated by the low linearity error labeled “reference backscatter.”
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Dynamic range tests of transmit and reference backscatter power, combining 860-, 910-, and 960-MHz results. Transmitting −2 to 29 dBm, linearity and noise errors are less than 0.1 dB. Backscatter noise is not zero-mean because the normalization is skewed by high-power compression.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The range of measurable <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the testbed depends largely on DUT placement in the test zone. Placing the tag co-polarized and in the main beam of the testbed antennas helps ensure turn-on and that backscatter is far above the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-\hbox{67 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-\hbox{67 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> testbed sensitivity. If <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx0} &lt; -\hbox{2 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx0} &lt; -\hbox{2 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the tag must be moved farther from the testbed antennas to maintain specified measurement linearity. Tags tested by the authors fall within <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-\hbox{30} (\hbox{dBm})^{2} &lt; B &lt; -\hbox{10} (\hbox{dBm})^{2}</span><script type="math/tex">-\hbox{30} (\hbox{dBm})^{2} &lt; B &lt; -\hbox{10} (\hbox{dBm})^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, all measurable near the main beam of the 8-dBi antennas at 1 m. Future tags with smaller <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> will tend toward smaller <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>To estimate the combined effects of noise and multipath in the anechoic environment, measurements of a commercial tag are swept with distance from the testbed antenna mount in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>. Deviation at each frequency point serves to demonstrate errors from a combination of thermal noise, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> truncation noise, and tag detuning by parasitic modes in the test zone. At worst, these errors have standard deviation of 0.1 dB. Assuming that they combine into normally distributed error, this is 0.2 dB standard uncertainty.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Mean and standard deviation of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> measured at eight positions in the test zone, from 60 to 120 cm (approximately <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">2\lambda</span><script type="math/tex">2\lambda</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">4\lambda</span><script type="math/tex">4\lambda</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) away from testbed antennas in 7.5 cm (approximately <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\lambda /4</span><script type="math/tex">\lambda /4</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) steps. At worst, standard deviation is below 0.1dB, which we believe is dominated by noise.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>These results contribute to the estimate of combined uncertainty of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> listed in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a>. The remaining uncertainty estimates are based on uncertainty analysis documentation provided by the manufacturer of the power sensor and network analyzer and with network analyzer verification impedance standards. The final combined uncertainty of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\pm {\hbox {0.45 dB}}</span><script type="math/tex">\pm {\hbox {0.45 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\pm 11\%</span><script type="math/tex">\pm 11\%</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) is computed from the quadrature sum of each uncertainty term as discussed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_4d">[22]</a> (which assumes the largest errors are normally distributed).
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table3"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table III </b>Expanded Uncertainty Estimates for Reported <span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-table-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-table-3-small.gif" alt="Table III" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Empirical Model Validation</h2></div><p>A tag built from a connectorized antenna and chip is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>. It enables separate antenna and chip impedance measurements to validate the model without probe and bonding parasitics. A commercially available tag chip package, marketed as compliant with <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_5">[5]</a>, is soldered directly onto an SMA connector. Its input impedance is transformed to near 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> within 860–960MHz by single-stub matching. The antenna is a commercially available dipole tuned to 910 MHz with an integrated 2:1 balun.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Connectorized “validation tag,” stub-matched to 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Measurements are calibrated at the dashed line. The 15-cm dipole has an integrated wideband 2:1 balun and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert \rho_{R}\vert &lt; -\hbox{10 {dB}}</span><script type="math/tex">\vert \rho_{R}\vert &lt; -\hbox{10 {dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> across 860–960 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>On-tag circuit parameter measurements for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are not typically practical, but are necessary here to validate our model and testbed. Other work has addressed the problem of measuring the power harvesting impedance state <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_5">[30]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref31" id="context_ref_31_5">[31]</a> with a network analyzer at a calibrated power level. Our network analyzer cannot excite or measure the time-varying reflective state <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{R}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, so we constructed a custom reflectometer like in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_5">[24]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref32" id="context_ref_32_5">[32]</a>.</p><p>First, the turn-on power into the chip network is determined by adjusting the power out of the interrogator in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9(a)</a> and measuring power at the given interface with a peak power sensor as described in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4b" class="fulltext-link">Section IV-B</a>. Measurements of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{L0}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{L0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{L}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, are performed at a fixed <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}</span><script type="math/tex">\bar {p}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by network analyzer with 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> input like the reader. The sensitivity of the chip network is then computed from a power sensor measurement at the coupler output <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm meas}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm meas}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L0} = P_{\rm meas}/(1-\vert \rho_{L0}\vert ^{2})</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L0} = P_{\rm meas}/(1-\vert \rho_{L0}\vert ^{2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, assuming that the coupler and reader are matched 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> sources. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> was within 0.2 dB of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-\hbox{13 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-\hbox{13 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> across the band.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Measurement configuration for (a) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{R}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is calibrated against (b)<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{L}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Power at network interfaces (dotted lines) are calibrated at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by power sensor.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>With <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{L0}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{L0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> known, reflections in each chip impedance state coupled into the spectrum analyzer can be compared to determine <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{R}</span><script type="math/tex">\rho_{R}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. If the coupler and instruments were ideally well matched, and the coupler had infinite directivity, the two reflection coefficients would be equal to the ratio of the complex IQ measurements <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{R}/V_{L}</span><script type="math/tex">V_{R}/V_{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at a given forward-wave voltage <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">V_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <disp-formula id="deqn25" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{{\rho_{R}}\over {\rho_{L}}} = {{V_{R}\over V_{\rm tx}}\over {V_{L} \over V_{\rm tx}}} = {{V_{R}}\over {V_{L}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(25)}}</span><script type="math/tex; mode=display">{{\rho_{R}}\over {\rho_{L}}} = {{V_{R}\over V_{\rm tx}}\over {V_{L} \over V_{\rm tx}}} = {{V_{R}}\over {V_{L}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(25)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{{\rho_{R}}\over {\rho_{L}}} = {{V_{R}\over V_{\rm tx}}\over {V_{L} \over V_{\rm tx}}} = {{V_{R}}\over {V_{L}}}.\eqno{\hbox{(25)}}</span></span></disp-formula>We also used the thorough directional coupler analysis in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref33" id="context_ref_33_5">[33]</a> to account for coupler directivity and mismatch uncertainty at the chip interface.</p><p>Computing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{\rm mod}(\bar p = {\hbox {0.8 dB}})</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{\rm mod}(\bar p = {\hbox {0.8 dB}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{L0}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{L0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn6" href="#deqn6" class="fulltext-link">(6)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn15" href="#deqn15" class="fulltext-link">(15)</a> with the circuit measurements gives the performance summarized in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>Measured efficiency of the tag pictured in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>, at turn-on and at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}= {\hbox {0.8 dB}}</span><script type="math/tex">\bar {p}= {\hbox {0.8 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Measured data shown in (a) the 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><script type="math/tex">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> Smith chart were used to compute (b) matching and modulation efficiencies <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{L0}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{L0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eta_{\rm mod}</span><script type="math/tex">\eta_{\rm mod}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> predicted by <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn17" href="#deqn17" class="fulltext-link">(17)</a> from these measurements are compared against testbed measurements in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11(a)</a> shows a frequency sweep with the validation tag on a polystyrene table (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\epsilon_{r} \approx 1</span><script type="math/tex">\epsilon_{r} \approx 1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11(b)</a> compares predicted <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the validation tag at three frequencies detuned by a 70 cm×70 cm aluminum plate. Circuit efficiencies were recalculated with measurements of the antenna reflection coefficient at each height. In all cases, the predicted <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> agree to within <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\pm {\hbox {0.35 dB}}</span><script type="math/tex">\pm {\hbox {0.35 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is within the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\pm {\hbox {0.5-dB}}</span><script type="math/tex">\pm {\hbox {0.5-dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> testbed uncertainty.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>Validation of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn17" href="#deqn17" class="fulltext-link">(17)</a> by measurements of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The setup detailed in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Sections IV</a> gives “testbed” <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. “On-tag” <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are from parameters in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>. Measurements in (a) an anechoic chamber normalize (b) detuning by an aluminum plate. All curves agree within the 0.5-dB testbed uncertainty.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>Realistic Link Testing</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6a"><h3>A. Testing in Detuning Conditions</h3><p>We begin with measurements performed with the testbed in an anechoic chamber. Results, shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a>, show frequency and linearity sweeps of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for a commercial tag. This tag is the subject of tests for the remainder of this section.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 12. </b><fig><p>Measurements of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for a commercial passive tag sample measured in an anechoic environment swept with (a) frequency (placed on polystyrene foam and a wooden box) and (b) power.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>Of course, operation in practice will involve fading. Previous experimental work into an equivalent parameter <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref34" id="context_ref_34_6a">[34]</a> already suggests only slight variations. However, these measurements use <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from a commercial reader's transmit power setting and received signal strength indicator (RSSI), for which we expect large linearity and repeatability errors. Therefore, with a focus on communication testing in reflective environments instead of sensing, and with the repeatable and linear testbed demonstrated by <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>, we empirically investigate the extent of this detuning error.</p><p>Consider backscatter “fading,” defined here as backscatter loss <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}/P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}/P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> normalized to free space behavior. The theory developed in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a> predicts that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> should only depend on <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z_{\rm ant}</span><script type="math/tex">Z_{\rm ant}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and not transmission loss. In contrast, the fading measurement depends on <i>both</i>. Therefore, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> should be more stable than fading in detuning conditions. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13</a> compares these near an aluminum plate in an anechoic chamber. Fading normalization is against measurements at the same tag position and operating point <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\bar {p}</span><script type="math/tex">\bar {p}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> but without the aluminum plate. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> converges to within 1 dB (25%) of its free space value beyond 15 cm above the plate. In contrast, fading is still 10 dB at 30 cm above the plate.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig13"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-13-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-13-small.gif" alt="Figure 13" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 13. </b><fig><p>Comparison of the stability of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and received backscattered power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the same commercial passive tag as <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a> near an aluminum plate.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>As a “realistic” example of this stability, tests were performed in a cluttered storage room. Ten positions were chosen for testing on top of metal scatterers strewn across a shelf, shown along with the tagged objects in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a>. The tag is attached atop each object in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14(c)</a>, 15 cm above shelf clutter. Results are given in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 15</a>. At this range, as in the anechoic chamber near the aluminum plate, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is stable to within 1 dB of its free space value.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig14"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-14-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-14-small.gif" alt="Figure 14" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 14. </b><fig><p>Shelf covered in metallic antenna mounting equipment to test detuning shown (a) from behind, with the ten test positions for the tagged object, and (b) from the side. Tests were performed on two tagged objects shown in (c): a polystyrene block (left), and a wooden test equipment box (right).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig15"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-15-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-15-small.gif" alt="Figure 15" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 15. </b><fig><p>Detuning effects in the storage room pictured in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a> with the tag placed on (a) polystyrene foam and (b) wood, normalized to measurements in a semi-anechoic chamber.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6b"><h3>B. Minimum Power Bounds from Measurements</h3><p>We now have enough test data to bound monostatic backscatter from the tag. Inserting results from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a> into <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn18" href="#deqn18" class="fulltext-link">(18)</a> gives contours for the bounds in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 16</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig16"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-16-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-16-small.gif" alt="Figure 16" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 16. </b><fig><p>Contours of minimum backscattered power from the tag sample into a monostatic reader in any environment, highlighting two example points. Estimates use measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a> with 2.5-dB margin to account for measurement uncertainty and tag impedance detuning effects by the environment.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 15</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">13</a> give us an idea for the stability of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{bs}]</span><script type="math/tex">\min [P_{bs}]</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. If foreign objects are kept separated by at least 15 cm from the tag, the minimum may be stable to within 1 dB of the indicated value. For a more conservative “worst case” estimate, a “detuning margin” greater than 0.8 dB can be subtracted from the contour in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 16</a>. More specific tests for stability of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</span><script type="math/tex">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be tailored by application.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6c"><h3>C. Reader Sensitivity</h3><p>Test standards <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_6c">[11]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_6c">[13]</a> do not yet define reader sensitivity (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) or suggest measurement techniques. For our tests, we arbitrarily define <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as “minimum power to achieve 50% inventory speed.” This could be defined differently for applications with different requirements. We performed inventories with the low-level reader protocol (LLRP), which is a standardized software protocol for controlling fixed readers that can operate with many commercial readers. We use an adapter to connect type-N connectors to our readers, which introduces small loss (below 1dB).</p><p>Contrasting measurement results from two different commercial readers in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 17</a>. We performed these <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> sweeps by attenuating the response from our reference backscatter circuit. Each reader was configured to transmit 30 dBm, but for each we measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}= \hbox{29.5 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}= \hbox{29.5 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The results suggest <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs0}=-\hbox{72 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs0}=-\hbox{72 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for “Reader 1” and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm bs0}=-\hbox{59 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm bs0}=-\hbox{59 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for “Reader 2.”
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig17"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-17-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-17-small.gif" alt="Figure 17" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 17. </b><fig><p>Inventory rate measurements for two commercial readers, frequency-hopping across 902–928 MHz. Results are averaged across 600 inventories after warming 1 h in ambient 21 °C at measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}=\hbox{29.5 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}=\hbox{29.5 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6d"><h3>D. Predicting Performance Degradation</h3><p>With device test data, we begin to demonstrate the system-level effects of return link performance. In the readers' 902–928-MHz band, <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 16</a> suggests minimum backscattered power at approximately <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-\hbox{59 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-\hbox{59 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The sensitivity of Reader 1 is therefore overspecified, 13 dB below <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</span><script type="math/tex">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This link should therefore be forward-link limited. Because of the tag's sharp turn-on characteristic, inventory performance should be reliable if the tag can turn on. The sensitivity of Reader 2 is equal to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{bs}]</span><script type="math/tex">\min [P_{bs}]</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, so we expect its inventory rate to deteriorate if the tag is near its turn-on threshold. In the presence of any detuning effects which reduce <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the curve in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 17</a> suggests rapid performance fall-off.</p><p>We measured inventory rate swept with reader-tag range in a warehouse, shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig18" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 18</a>. Both the reader antenna (a 6-dBi circularly polarized patch antenna) and the tag (mounted on foam) were 1 m above a concrete floor and propagated using a line-of-sight nethod. Total interference within all 902–928-MHz channels with this antenna was below <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-\hbox{80 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">-\hbox{80 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with the spectrum analyzer.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig18"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-18-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-18-small.gif" alt="Figure 18" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 18. </b><fig><p>Inventory rates reported by the frequency-hopping readers of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 17</a>, measured in a warehouse environment. Rates are averaged across all channels containing detected tag responses.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>As expected, Reader 1 reported an effectively constant inventory rate when the tag turned on. Reader 2 shows slightly decreased inventory performance at long range, with an outlier at 20 m that may be caused by detuning or spurious interference. The trend is not monotonic because of multipath effects.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6e"><h3>E. Performance Trends</h3><p>Reader 2 performance at distance did degrade, but the effect was slight—inventory rate was typically above 60% when the tag turned on. It is tempting to conclude from this that return link performance may not be important.</p><p>To give some context, measurements of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for some other tag samples are plotted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 19</a> against estimated year of manufacture. Because tag chips' <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{L0}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{L0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> has fallen, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is falling too—roughly 10 dB in five years. At <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}=\hbox{29.5 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}=\hbox{29.5 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the newest tag would return a minimum <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{\rm bs}]=-\hbox{62 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">\min [P_{\rm bs}]=-\hbox{62 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. According to <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 17</a>, Reader 2 would detect this tag at a mere 3% of its maximum rate. If future tags continue the trend of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 19</a>, the return link will soon become the dominant constraint upon passive RFID communication.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig19"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-19-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6226493/6200004/6200004-fig-19-small.gif" alt="Figure 19" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 19. </b><fig><p>Sample tags' <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, measured in an anechoic chamber plotted against estimated year of manufacture. The size of each circle is proportional to the size of the tag. The black line at each point shows the range of measured <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> across 860–960 MHz. Each color represents a different manufacturer.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6200004/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec7"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VII.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>This paper has considered in detail how the parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can describe the balance between forward and return link performance. We have validated the proposed relationship to within <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\pm {\hbox {0.5 dB}}</span><script type="math/tex">\pm {\hbox {0.5 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> measurement uncertainty with a novel backscatter measurement calibration. We have also demonstrated how the parameter applies to specifying adequate monostatic reader sensitivity to help ensure reliable inventory performance in realistic environments.</p><p>This model and calibration device together enabled improved measurement accuracy. Standardized <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma_{\Delta}</span><script type="math/tex">\sigma_{\Delta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> tests, with estimated uncertainty of 2 dB, are dominated by uncertainty involving antenna radiation characteristics, which are difficult and costly to measure. Even without recalibrating demodulated backscatter from a spectrum analyzer, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">B</span><script type="math/tex">B</script></tex-math></inline-formula> would have uncertainty of the order of 1 dB. With the new calibration method, this is further improved to within <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\pm {\hbox {0.5 dB}}</span><script type="math/tex">\pm {\hbox {0.5 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Our testbed is more complex and costly than necessary for commercial testing. A simpler monostatic test setup would require only: 1) calibrated <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>; 2) detection with a “reasonably linear” IQ demodulator; and 3) the calibration device proposed in this paper. In practice, this could be nearly as accurate as that proposed in this paper. One-time calibration with the new reference device needs a single use of a network analyzer.</p><p>If tag and reader manufacturers provided return link characterization data, customers could predict return link performance before purchasing equipment. Tag vendors wishing to offer meaningful performance data can specify the minimum backscattering bound for parameters based on anticipated uses under national regulations. For example, in the United States, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</span><script type="math/tex">\min [P_{\rm bs}]</script></tex-math></inline-formula> might be specified across 902–928 MHz at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm tx}=\hbox{33 dBm}</span><script type="math/tex">P_{\rm tx}=\hbox{33 dBm}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (anticipating regulatory compliance with 3 dB of cable loss). A datasheet could provide values with the tag mounted on a variety of different objects.</p></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
